### YouTube Data API v3 - Getting Started

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/getting-started

This section outlines the essential steps to begin using the YouTube Data API v3, including account setup, project creation, API enablement, and authentication.

```APIDOC
## Getting Started with YouTube Data API v3

### Description
To use the YouTube Data API v3, developers need to complete several setup steps to ensure their application can access and interact with YouTube data.

### Prerequisites
1.  **Google Account**: Required for accessing the Google API Console and managing API keys.
2.  **Google Developers Console Project**: Create a project to organize your API usage and obtain credentials.
3.  **Enable YouTube Data API v3**: Ensure the API is enabled for your project in the Google Developers Console.
4.  **Authentication**: Implement OAuth 2.0 for methods requiring user authorization.
5.  **Client Library**: Consider using a client library to simplify API integration.
6.  **JSON Familiarity**: Understand the JSON data format for request and response payloads.

### Steps
1.  **Obtain Google Account and API Console Access**
    *   Sign in with your Google Account.
    *   Navigate to the Google Developers Console.
2.  **Create a Project and Obtain Credentials**
    *   Create a new project in the Developers Console.
    *   Generate API credentials (e.g., API key, OAuth 2.0 client ID).
3.  **Enable the YouTube Data API v3**
    *   In your project, go to 'Enabled APIs'.
    *   Find 'YouTube Data API v3' and ensure its status is 'ON'.
4.  **Implement Authentication (if needed)**
    *   For user-specific data, implement the OAuth 2.0 flow as described in the authentication guide.
5.  **Choose a Client Library**
    *   Select a client library for your programming language to streamline development.

### Resources
*   [Google API Console](https://console.developers.google.com/)
*   [YouTube Data API v3 Authentication Guide](https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/guides/auth)
*   [JSON Official Website](http://www.json.org/)
```

These quickstart guides provide instructions on setting up a simple application to make YouTube Data API requests. They are available for Android, Apps Script, Go, Java, JavaScript, Node.js, PHP, Python, and Ruby.

```java
// Placeholder for Java Quickstart guide code.
// Actual code would be in a separate file and involve setting up the YouTube Data API client.
public class YouTubeQuickstart {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println("YouTube Data API v3 Java Quickstart placeholder.");
        // Steps typically involve:
        // 1. Setting up the build.gradle file.
        // 2. Creating a GoogleCredential object.
        // 3. Building the YouTube service object.
        // 4. Making API calls (e.g., channels.list).
    }
}
```

```javascript
// Placeholder for JavaScript Quickstart guide code (Node.js example).

const { google } = require('googleapis');

async function quickstart() {
  console.log('YouTube Data API v3 JavaScript (Node.js) Quickstart placeholder.');
  // Steps typically involve:
  // 1. Installing the googleapis package: npm install googleapis
  // 2. Authenticating the user (OAuth2).
  // 3. Creating a YouTube service object.
  // 4. Making API calls (e.g., search.list).
}

quickstart().catch(console.error);

```

```php
<?php
/**
 * Placeholder for PHP Quickstart guide code.
 * Actual code would be in a separate file and involve setting up the YouTube Data API client.
 */
require_once __DIR__ . '/vendor/autoload.php';

function quickstart_php() {
    echo 'YouTube Data API v3 PHP Quickstart placeholder.\n';
    // Steps typically involve:
    // 1. Installing the google/apiclient library: composer require google/apiclient
    // 2. Setting up client with credentials (API key or OAuth2).
    // 3. Creating a YouTube service object.
    // 4. Making API calls (e.g., playlists.list).
}

quickstart_php();
?>
```

```python
# Placeholder for Python Quickstart guide code.
# Actual code would be in a separate file and involve setting up the YouTube Data API client.
from googleapiclient.discovery import build

API_KEY = 'YOUR_API_KEY' # Or use OAuth2 for authenticated requests

def quickstart_python():
    print('YouTube Data API v3 Python Quickstart placeholder.')
    # Steps typically involve:
    # 1. Installing the google-api-python-client library: pip install --upgrade google-api-python-client
    # 2. Building the YouTube service object.
    # 3. Making API calls (e.g., videos.list).
    try:
        youtube = build('youtube', 'v3', developerKey=API_KEY)
        # Example API call (replace with actual method)
        # request = youtube.channels().list(part='snippet,statistics', id='UC_x5XG1OV2P6uZZ5FSM9Ttw')
        # response = request.execute()
        # print(response)
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"An error occurred: {e}")

quickstart_python()

```

### .NET Client Library Example

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/docs/playlistItems/list

This .NET code sample demonstrates how to retrieve a list of videos uploaded to the authenticated user's channel using the Google API Client Library for .NET. It utilizes `Channels.List` to get channel details and implies subsequent use of `PlaylistItems.List` (though not fully detailed in the provided snippet).

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/channels

### Description
Retrieves a list of channels that match the specified query parameters. This is used here to get the channel ID of the authenticated user.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/channels

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **part** (string) - Required - The part of the channel resource that you want the channel to return.
- **mine** (boolean) - Required - Indicates that you want to retrieve channels associated with the authenticated user.

### Request Example
```csharp
// This is a conceptual representation, actual call is within the C# code.
// var channelsListRequest = youtubeService.Channels.List("contentDetails");
// channelsListRequest.Mine = true;
// var response = await channelsListRequest.ExecuteAsync();
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **items** (array) - The channel resources.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "kind": "youtube#channelListResponse",
  "etag": "...",
  "items": [
    {
      "kind": "youtube#channel",
      "etag": "...",
      "id": "CHANNEL_ID",
      "contentDetails": {
        "relatedPlaylists": {
          "likes": "...",
          "favorites": "...",
          "uploads": "UPLOADS_PLAYLIST_ID",
          "watchHistory": "..."
        }
      }
    }
  ]
}
```

## GET /youtube/v3/playlistItems

### Description
Retrieves a collection of playlist items in the specified playlist. This endpoint would be used after obtaining the `UPLOADS_PLAYLIST_ID` from the `channels.list` response to fetch the actual videos.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/playlistItems

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **part** (string) - Required - The part of the playlist item resource, which you can use to view or modify its properties.
- **playlistId** (string) - Required - The playlistId of the playlist for which to retrieve playlist items.
- **pageToken** (string) - Optional - The nextPageToken value returned from a previous Query call. 

### Request Example
```csharp
// This is a conceptual representation, actual call is within the C# code.
// var playlistItemsRequest = youtubeService.PlaylistItems.List(part);
// playlistItemsRequest.PlaylistId = playlistId;
// if (!string.IsNullOrEmpty(pageToken)) {
//     playlistItemsRequest.PageToken = pageToken;
// }
// var response = await playlistItemsRequest.ExecuteAsync();
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **items** (array) - The playlist items.
- **nextPageToken** (string) - The token that can be used to retrieve the next page of results.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "kind": "youtube#playlistItemListResponse",
  "etag": "...",
  "items": [
    {
      "kind": "youtube#playlistItem",
      "etag": "...",
      "id": "...",
      "snippet": {
        "publishedAt": "...",
        "channelId": "...",
        "title": "Video Title",
        "description": "...",
        "thumbnails": { ... },
        "channelTitle": "...",
        "playlistId": "...",
        "position": 0,
        "resourceId": {
          "kind": "youtube#video",
          "videoId": "VIDEO_ID"
        }
      }
    }
  ],
  "nextPageToken": "..."
}
```
```

### GET /youtube/v3/videos - Example 1: Including multiple parts

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/getting-started_hl=id

This example demonstrates retrieving a video resource and includes the `snippet`, `contentDetails`, `statistics`, and `status` parts in the API response.

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/videos

### Description
Retrieves a video resource, specifying which parts of the resource to include in the response.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/videos

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **id** (string) - Required - The ID of the video to retrieve.
- **key** (string) - Required - Your API key.
- **part** (string) - Required - Comma-separated list of video resource parts to include in the response (e.g., `snippet`, `contentDetails`, `statistics`, `status`).

### Request Example
```
https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos?id=7lCDEYXw3mM&key=YOUR_API_KEY&part=snippet,contentDetails,statistics,status
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **kind** (string) - The type of resource returned.
- **etag** (string) - The ETag of the response.
- **videos** (array) - An array of video resources.
  - **id** (string) - The ID of the video.
  - **kind** (string) - The type of video resource.
  - **etag** (string) - The ETag of the video resource.
  - **snippet** (object) - Contains details about the video's metadata.
    - **publishedAt** (string) - The date and time the video was published.
    - **channelId** (string) - The ID of the channel that published the video.
    - **title** (string) - The title of the video.
    - **description** (string) - The description of the video.
    - **thumbnails** (object) - Thumbnails for the video.
    - **categoryId** (string) - The ID of the video's category.
  - **contentDetails** (object) - Contains details about the video's content.
    - **duration** (string) - The duration of the video.
    - **aspectRatio** (string) - The aspect ratio of the video.
  - **statistics** (object) - Contains statistics about the video.
    - **viewCount** (string) - The number of views.
    - **likeCount** (string) - The number of likes.
    - **dislikeCount** (string) - The number of dislikes.
    - **favoriteCount** (string) - The number of favorites.
    - **commentCount** (string) - The number of comments.
  - **status** (object) - Contains the status of the video.
    - **uploadStatus** (string) - The upload status of the video.
    - **privacyStatus** (string) - The privacy status of the video.

#### Response Example
```json
{
 "kind": "youtube#videoListResponse",
 "etag": "\"UCBpFjp2h75_b92t44sqraUcyu0/sDAlsG9NGKfr6v5AlPZKSEZdtqA\"",
 "videos": [
  {
   "id": "7lCDEYXw3mM",
   "kind": "youtube#video",
   "etag": "\"UCBpFjp2h75_b92t44sqraUcyu0/iYynQR8AtacsFUwWmrVaw4Smb_Q\"",
   "snippet": {
    "publishedAt": "2012-06-20T22:45:24.000Z",
    "channelId": "UC_x5XG1OV2P6uZZ5FSM9Ttw",
    "title": "Google I/O 101: Q&A On Using Google APIs",
    "description": "Antonio Fuentes speaks to us and takes questions on working with Google APIs and OAuth 2.0.",
    "thumbnails": {
     "default": {
      "url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/default.jpg"
     },
     "medium": {
      "url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/mqdefault.jpg"
     },
     "high": {
      "url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/hqdefault.jpg"
     }
    },
    "categoryId": "28"
   },
   "contentDetails": {
    "duration": "PT15M51S",
    "aspectRatio": "RATIO_16_9"
   },
   "statistics": {
    "viewCount": "3057",
    "likeCount": "25",
    "dislikeCount": "0",
    "favoriteCount": "17",
    "commentCount": "12"
   },
   "status": {
    "uploadStatus": "STATUS_PROCESSED",
    "privacyStatus": "PRIVACY_PUBLIC"
   }
  }
 ]
}
```
```

### GET /youtube/v3/videos - Retrieve Video Resource with Specific Parts

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/getting-started

This example demonstrates how to retrieve a video resource and specifies which parts of the resource should be included in the API response using the 'part' parameter. It includes 'snippet', 'contentDetails', 'statistics', and 'status'.

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/videos

### Description
Retrieves a video resource, allowing specification of which resource parts to include in the response.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **id** (string) - Required - The ID of the video to retrieve.
- **key** (string) - Required - Your API key.
- **part** (string) - Required - Comma-separated list of resource parts to include in the response (e.g., snippet,contentDetails,statistics,status).

### Request Example
```
GET https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos?id=7lCDEYXw3mM&key=YOUR_API_KEY&part=snippet,contentDetails,statistics,status
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **kind** (string) - The type of resource returned.
- **etag** (string) - The ETag of the response.
- **videos** (array) - A list of video resources matching the request.
  - **id** (string) - The ID of the video.
  - **kind** (string) - The type of video resource.
  - **etag** (string) - The ETag of the video resource.
  - **snippet** (object) - The snippet object containing basic details about the video.
  - **contentDetails** (object) - The contentDetails object containing information about the video's duration and aspect ratio.
  - **statistics** (object) - The statistics object containing view, like, dislike, favorite, and comment counts.
  - **status** (object) - The status object containing upload and privacy status.

#### Response Example
```json
{
 "kind": "youtube#videoListResponse",
 "etag": "\"UCBpFjp2h75_b92t44sqraUcyu0/sDAlsG9NGKfr6v5AlPZKSEZdtqA\"",
 "videos": [
  {
   "id": "7lCDEYXw3mM",
   "kind": "youtube#video",
   "etag": "\"UCBpFjp2h75_b92t44sqraUcyu0/iYynQR8AtacsFUwWmrVaw4Smb_Q\"",
   "snippet": {
    "publishedAt": "2012-06-20T22:45:24.000Z",
    "channelId": "UC_x5XG1OV2P6uZZ5FSM9Ttw",
    "title": "Google I/O 101: Q&A On Using Google APIs",
    "description": "Antonio Fuentes speaks to us and takes questions on working with Google APIs and OAuth 2.0.",
    "thumbnails": {
     "default": {"url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/default.jpg"},
     "medium": {"url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/mqdefault.jpg"},
     "high": {"url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/hqdefault.jpg"}
    },
    "categoryId": "28"
   },
   "contentDetails": {
    "duration": "PT15M51S",
    "aspectRatio": "RATIO_16_9"
   },
   "statistics": {
    "viewCount": "3057",
    "likeCount": "25",
    "dislikeCount": "0",
    "favoriteCount": "17",
    "commentCount": "12"
   },
   "status": {
    "uploadStatus": "STATUS_PROCESSED",
    "privacyStatus": "PRIVACY_PUBLIC"
   }
  }
 ]
}
```
```

### YouTube API v3 Channels List with Node.js Code Sample

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=zh-tw

Demonstrates how to use the channels.list method in the YouTube API v3 with Node.js. This sample includes utility functions for parameter handling, providing a starting point for Node.js applications interacting with the API. It is similar to the Node.js quickstart guide but contains additional utility functions.

```javascript
function removeEmptyParameters(parameters) {
  const newParameters = {};
  for (const key in parameters) {
    if (parameters.hasOwnProperty(key) && parameters[key]) {
      newParameters[key] = parameters[key];
    }
  }
  return newParameters;
}

// Example usage:
// const params = {
//   part: 'snippet',
//   id: 'UCBR8-60-B28hp2BmDPdntcQ'
// };
// const cleanedParams = removeEmptyParameters(params);
// console.log(cleanedParams);

```

### Go Client Library Example

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/docs/playlistItems/list

This Go code sample demonstrates how to retrieve a list of videos uploaded to the authenticated user's channel. It first fetches the channel's upload playlist ID using `channels.list` and then retrieves the playlist items using `playlistItems.list`.

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/playlistItems

### Description
Retrieves a collection of playlist items in the specified playlist. This is used here to get videos uploaded to a channel.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/playlistItems

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **part** (string) - Required - The part of the playlist item resource, which you can use to view or modify its properties.
- **playlistId** (string) - Required - The playlistId of the playlist for which to retrieve playlist items.
- **pageToken** (string) - Optional - The nextPageToken value returned from a previous Query call. 

### Request Example
```go
// This is a conceptual representation, actual call is within the Go code.
// service.PlaylistItems.List("snippet").PlaylistId(playlistId).PageToken(pageToken).Do()
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **items** (array) - The playlist items.
- **nextPageToken** (string) - The token that can be used to retrieve the next page of results.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "kind": "youtube#playlistItemListResponse",
  "etag": "...",
  "items": [
    {
      "kind": "youtube#playlistItem",
      "etag": "...",
      "id": "...",
      "snippet": {
        "publishedAt": "...",
        "channelId": "...",
        "title": "Video Title",
        "description": "...",
        "thumbnails": { ... },
        "channelTitle": "...",
        "playlistId": "...",
        "position": 0,
        "resourceId": {
          "kind": "youtube#video",
          "videoId": "VIDEO_ID"
        }
      }
    }
  ],
  "nextPageToken": "..."
}
```

## GET /youtube/v3/channels

### Description
Retrieves a list of channels that match the specified query parameters. This is used here to get the channel ID of the authenticated user.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/channels

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **part** (string) - Required - The part of the channel resource that you want the channel to return.
- **mine** (boolean) - Required - Indicates that you want to retrieve channels associated with the authenticated user.

### Request Example
```go
// This is a conceptual representation, actual call is within the Go code.
// service.Channels.List("contentDetails").Mine(true).Do()
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **items** (array) - The channel resources.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "kind": "youtube#channelListResponse",
  "etag": "...",
  "items": [
    {
      "kind": "youtube#channel",
      "etag": "...",
      "id": "CHANNEL_ID",
      "contentDetails": {
        "relatedPlaylists": {
          "likes": "...",
          "favorites": "...",
          "uploads": "UPLOADS_PLAYLIST_ID",
          "watchHistory": "..."
        }
      }
    }
  ]
}
```

### Go Example for activities.insert Method

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=tr

Provides a Go code sample for inserting activities into YouTube. This snippet demonstrates how to interact with the activities.insert method.

```Go
package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"log"

	"google.golang.org/api/youtube/v3"
)

func main() {
	// Assume "youtubeService" is an initialized youtube.Service object
	youtubeService, err := youtube.New(nil) // Replace with your authenticated client
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error creating YouTube client: %v", err)
	}

	activity := &youtube.Activity{
		Snippet: &youtube.ActivitySnippet{
			Title:       "My Awesome Activity",
			Description: "This is a description of my activity.",
		},
		// Other properties can be set here as needed
	}

	call := youtubeService.Activities.Insert("snippet", activity)
	_, err = call.Do()
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error inserting activity: %v", err)
	}

	fmt.Println("Activity inserted successfully!")
}
```

### YouTube Data API v3 - Core Concepts

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/live/getting-started

This section outlines the fundamental concepts and prerequisites for using the YouTube Data API v3, including account setup, application registration, and understanding JSON.

```APIDOC
## Getting Started with YouTube Data API v3

### Description
Before you start using the YouTube Data API v3, ensure you have a Google Account, register your application, and enable the YouTube Data API v3 in the Google API Console. Familiarize yourself with the JSON data format.

### Prerequisites
1. **Google Account**: Required for accessing the Google API Console, requesting an API key, and registering your application.
2. **Application Registration**: Register your application with Google to submit API requests.
3. **Enable YouTube Data API v3**: In the API Console, select your project and enable the YouTube Data API v3. For content partners, also enable the YouTube Content ID API.
4. **JSON Data Format**: Understand the basics of JSON (JavaScript Object Notation) for data exchange.

### Resources
- **liveBroadcast**: Represents a YouTube broadcast event, including metadata specific to live streaming.
- **liveStream**: Contains information about the video stream being transmitted to YouTube.
- **cuepoint**: Inserts a cuepoint into the broadcast stream, potentially triggering ad breaks.
- **video**: Represents a single YouTube video. A `liveBroadcast` is an extension of this resource.
- **videoAdvertisingOptions**: Defines advertising settings for a video or broadcast.
- **asset**: Represents a piece of intellectual property (e.g., a movie, show episode).
- **claim**: Links a video to an asset, identifying ownership.
- **policy**: Defines rules for content visibility on YouTube.
```

--------------------------------

### YouTube Data API v3: Quota Cost Example for Subscriptions Insert

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=th

This snippet provides an example of quota cost calculation for the subscriptions.insert method and its associated resource parts. The example illustrates how different parts contribute to the total quota usage.

```text
subscriptions.insert method quota cost: ~50 units.
Subscription resource parts (snippet, contentDetails, subscriberSnippet): 2 units each.
```

### Go Example for videos.insert Method

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=tr

Illustrates how to insert a video using the YouTube Data API v3 in Go. This snippet covers the essential steps for the videos.insert method.

```Go
package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"log"
	"os"

	"google.golang.org/api/youtube/v3"
)

func main() {
	// Assume "youtubeService" is an initialized youtube.Service object
	youtubeService, err := youtube.New(nil) // Replace with your authenticated client
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error creating YouTube client: %v", err)
	}

	video := &youtube.Video{
		Snippet: &youtube.VideoSnippet{
			Title:       "My Awesome Video",
			Description: "This is a description of my video.",
			CategoryId:  "22", // Example category ID for 'People & Blogs'
		},
		Status: &youtube.VideoStatus{
			PrivacyStatus: "private", // or "public", "unlisted"
		},
	}

	file, err := os.Open("path/to/your/video.mp4") // Replace with the path to your video file
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error opening video file: %v", err)
	}
	defer file.Close()

	contentDetails := &youtube.VideoContentDetails{}

	call := youtubeService.Videos.Insert("snippet,status,contentDetails", video)
	call.Media(contentDetails, file)

	_, err = call.Do()
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error inserting video: %v", err)
	}

	fmt.Println("Video uploaded successfully!")
}
```

--------------------------------

### GET /youtube/v3/videos - Filter Response Fields with 'fields'

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/getting-started

This example demonstrates how to use the 'fields' parameter to precisely control which properties are returned in the API response, excluding metadata like 'kind' and 'etag'.

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/videos

### Description
Retrieves a video resource, using the 'fields' parameter to exclude metadata properties like 'kind' and 'etag' from the response.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **id** (string) - Required - The ID of the video to retrieve.
- **key** (string) - Required - Your API key.
- **part** (string) - Required - Comma-separated list of resource parts to include in the response (e.g., snippet,statistics).
- **fields** (string) - Optional - Specifies which fields to return in the response (e.g., items(id,snippet,statistics)).

### Request Example
```
GET https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos?id=7lCDEYXw3mM&key=YOUR_API_KEY&part=snippet,statistics&fields=items(id,snippet,statistics)
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **videos** (array) - A list of video resources matching the request, with specified fields only.
  - **id** (string) - The ID of the video.
  - **snippet** (object) - The snippet object containing basic details about the video.
  - **statistics** (object) - The statistics object containing view, like, dislike, favorite, and comment counts.

#### Response Example
```json
{
 "videos": [
  {
   "id": "7lCDEYXw3mM",
   "snippet": {
    "publishedAt": "2012-06-20T22:45:24.000Z",
    "channelId": "UC_x5XG1OV2P6uZZ5FSM9Ttw",
    "title": "Google I/O 101: Q&A On Using Google APIs",
    "description": "Antonio Fuentes speaks to us and takes questions on working with Google APIs and OAuth 2.0.",
    "thumbnails": {
     "default": {"url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/default.jpg"},
     "medium": {"url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/mqdefault.jpg"},
     "high": {"url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/hqdefault.jpg"}
    },
    "categoryId": "28"
   },
   "statistics": {
    "viewCount": "3057",
    "likeCount": "25",
    "dislikeCount": "0",
    "favoriteCount": "17",
    "commentCount": "12"
   }
  }
 ]

### Go Example for search.list Method

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=tr

Demonstrates how to perform searches using the YouTube Data API v3 in Go. This snippet illustrates the usage of the search.list method with parameters for live broadcast content.

```Go
package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"log"

	"google.golang.org/api/youtube/v3"
)

func main() {
	// Assume "youtubeService" is an initialized youtube.Service object
	youtubeService, err := youtube.New(nil) // Replace with your authenticated client
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error creating YouTube client: %v", err)
	}

	call := youtubeService.Search.List("snippet")
	call.Q("live streams")
	call.Type("video")
	call.LiveBroadcastContent("upcoming") // Can be "upcoming", "active", or "none"
	call.MaxResults(10)

	response, err := call.Do()
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error performing search: %v", err)
	}

	fmt.Println("Search results for upcoming live streams:")
	for _, item := range response.Items {
		fmt.Printf("- %s (ID: %s)\n", item.Snippet.Title, item.Id.VideoId)
	}
}
```

### GET /youtube/v3/videos - Example 2: Excluding specific parts

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/getting-started_hl=id

This example modifies the `part` parameter to exclude `contentDetails` and `status` properties from the video resource response.

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/videos

### Description
Retrieves a video resource, excluding specific parts like `contentDetails` and `status` by modifying the `part` parameter.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/videos

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **id** (string) - Required - The ID of the video to retrieve.
- **key** (string) - Required - Your API key.
- **part** (string) - Required - Comma-separated list of video resource parts to include in the response (e.g., `snippet`, `statistics`).

### Request Example
```
https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos?id=7lCDEYXw3mM&key=YOUR_API_KEY&part=snippet,statistics
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **kind** (string) - The type of resource returned.
- **etag** (string) - The ETag of the response.
- **videos** (array) - An array of video resources.
  - **id** (string) - The ID of the video.
  - **kind** (string) - The type of video resource.
  - **etag** (string) - The ETag of the video resource.
  - **snippet** (object) - Contains details about the video's metadata.
    - **publishedAt** (string) - The date and time the video was published.
    - **channelId** (string) - The ID of the channel that published the video.
    - **title** (string) - The title of the video.
    - **description** (string) - The description of the video.
    - **thumbnails** (object) - Thumbnails for the video.
    - **categoryId** (string) - The ID of the video's category.
  - **statistics** (object) - Contains statistics about the video.
    - **viewCount** (string) - The number of views.
    - **likeCount** (string) - The number of likes.
    - **dislikeCount** (string) - The number of dislikes.
    - **favoriteCount** (string) - The number of favorites.
    - **commentCount** (string) - The number of comments.

#### Response Example
```json
{
 "kind": "youtube#videoListResponse",
 "etag": "\"UCBpFjp2h75_b92t44sqraUcyu0/sDAlsG9NGKfr6v5AlPZKSEZdtqA\"",
 "videos": [
  {
   "id": "7lCDEYXw3mM",
   "kind": "youtube#video",
   "etag": "\"UCBpFjp2h75_b92t44sqraUcyu0/iYynQR8AtacsFUwWmrVaw4Smb_Q\"",
   "snippet": {
    "publishedAt": "2012-06-20T22:45:24.000Z",
    "channelId": "UC_x5XG1OV2P6uZZ5FSM9Ttw",
    "title": "Google I/O 101: Q&A On Using Google APIs",
    "description": "Antonio Fuentes speaks to us and takes questions on working with Google APIs and OAuth 2.0.",
    "thumbnails": {
     "default": {
      "url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/default.jpg"
     },
     "medium": {
      "url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/mqdefault.jpg"
     },
     "high": {
      "url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/hqdefault.jpg"
     }
    },
    "categoryId": "28"
   },
   "statistics": {
    "viewCount": "3057",
    "likeCount": "25",
    "dislikeCount": "0",
    "favoriteCount": "17",
    "commentCount": "12"
   }
  }
 ]
}
```
```

### GET /youtube/v3/videos - Customize Response Parts

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/getting-started

This example shows how to modify the 'part' parameter to exclude specific properties like 'contentDetails' and 'status' from the API response, reducing the amount of data transferred.

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/videos

### Description
Retrieves a video resource, excluding specific parts like 'contentDetails' and 'status' by modifying the 'part' parameter.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **id** (string) - Required - The ID of the video to retrieve.
- **key** (string) - Required - Your API key.
- **part** (string) - Required - Comma-separated list of resource parts to include in the response (e.g., snippet,statistics).

### Request Example
```
GET https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos?id=7lCDEYXw3mM&key=YOUR_API_KEY&part=snippet,statistics
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **kind** (string) - The type of resource returned.
- **etag** (string) - The ETag of the response.
- **videos** (array) - A list of video resources matching the request.
  - **id** (string) - The ID of the video.
  - **kind** (string) - The type of video resource.
  - **etag** (string) - The ETag of the video resource.
  - **snippet** (object) - The snippet object containing basic details about the video.
  - **statistics** (object) - The statistics object containing view, like, dislike, favorite, and comment counts.

#### Response Example
```json
{
 "kind": "youtube#videoListResponse",
 "etag": "\"UCBpFjp2h75_b92t44sqraUcyu0/sDAlsG9NGKfr6v5AlPZKSEZdtqA\"",
 "videos": [
  {
   "id": "7lCDEYXw3mM",
   "kind": "youtube#video",
   "etag": "\"UCBpFjp2h75_b92t44sqraUcyu0/iYynQR8AtacsFUwWmrVaw4Smb_Q\"",
   "snippet": {
    "publishedAt": "2012-06-20T22:45:24.000Z",
    "channelId": "UC_x5XG1OV2P6uZZ5FSM9Ttw",
    "title": "Google I/O 101: Q&A On Using Google APIs",
    "description": "Antonio Fuentes speaks to us and takes questions on working with Google APIs and OAuth 2.0.",
    "thumbnails": {
     "default": {"url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/default.jpg"},
     "medium": {"url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/mqdefault.jpg"},
     "high": {"url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/hqdefault.jpg"}
    },
    "categoryId": "28"
   },
   "statistics": {
    "viewCount": "3057",
    "likeCount": "25",
    "dislikeCount": "0",
    "favoriteCount": "17",
    "commentCount": "12"
   }
  }
 ]
}
```

### GET /youtube/v3/videos - Example 4: Nested fields selection

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/getting-started_hl=id

This example further refines the `fields` parameter to select specific nested properties within the `snippet` and `statistics` parts of the video resource.

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/videos

### Description
Retrieves a video resource, using the `fields` parameter to select specific nested properties within the `snippet` and `statistics` parts, while also specifying the `part` parameter.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/videos

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **id** (string) - Required - The ID of the video to retrieve.
- **key** (string) - Required - Your API key.
- **part** (string) - Required - Comma-separated list of video resource parts to include in the response (e.g., `snippet`, `statistics`).
- **fields** (string) - Optional - Specifies which fields of the resource to return. Use dot notation for nested fields and parentheses for arrays.

### Request Example
```
https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos?id=7lCDEYXw3mM&key=YOUR_API_KEY&fields=items(id,snippet(channelId,title,categoryId),statistics)&part=snippet,statistics
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **videos** (array) - An array of video resources.
  - **id** (string) - The ID of the video.
  - **snippet** (object) - Contains selected details about the video's metadata.
    - **channelId** (string) - The ID of the channel that published the video.
    - **title** (string) - The title of the video.
    - **categoryId** (string) - The ID of the video's category.
  - **statistics** (object) - Contains statistics about the video.
    - **viewCount** (string) - The number of views.
    - **likeCount** (string) - The number of likes.
    - **dislikeCount** (string) - The number of dislikes.
    - **favoriteCount** (string) - The number of favorites.
    - **commentCount** (string) - The number of comments.

#### Response Example
```json
{
 "videos": [
  {
   "id": "7lCDEYXw3mM",
   "snippet": {
    "channelId": "UC_x5XG1OV2P6uZZ5FSM9Ttw",
    "title": "Google I/O 101: Q&A On Using Google APIs",
    "categoryId": "28"
   },
   "statistics": {
    "viewCount": "3057",
    "likeCount": "25",
    "dislikeCount": "0",
    "favoriteCount": "17",
    "commentCount": "12"
   }
  }
 ]
}
```
```

--------------------------------

### Go Example for playlistItems.list Method

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=tr

Provides a Go code sample for listing playlist items using the YouTube Data API v3. This snippet demonstrates how to use the playlistItems.list method with relevant parameters.

```Go
package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"log"

	"google.golang.org/api/youtube/v3"
)

func main() {
	// Assume "youtubeService" is an initialized youtube.Service object
	youtubeService, err := youtube.New(nil) // Replace with your authenticated client
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error creating YouTube client: %v", err)
	}

	playlistID := "YOUR_PLAYLIST_ID" // Replace with the playlist ID

	call := youtubeService.PlaylistItems.List("snippet,contentDetails")
	call.PlaylistId(playlistID)
	call.MaxResults(50)

	response, err := call.Do()
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error listing playlist items: %v", err)
	}

	fmt.Printf("Playlist items for playlist %s:\n", playlistID)
	for _, item := range response.Items {
		fmt.Printf("- %s (%s)\n", item.Snippet.Title, item.Id)
	}
}
```

### GET /youtube/v3/videos - Example 3: Using fields to exclude properties

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/getting-started_hl=id

This example adds the `fields` parameter to the request to remove all `kind` and `etag` properties from the video resource response.

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/videos

### Description
Retrieves a video resource, using the `fields` parameter to exclude specific properties like `kind` and `etag` from the response.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/videos

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **id** (string) - Required - The ID of the video to retrieve.
- **key** (string) - Required - Your API key.
- **part** (string) - Required - Comma-separated list of video resource parts to include in the response (e.g., `snippet`, `statistics`).
- **fields** (string) - Optional - Specifies which fields of the resource to return. Use dot notation for nested fields and parentheses for arrays.

### Request Example
```
https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos?id=7lCDEYXw3mM&key=YOUR_API_KEY&part=snippet,statistics&fields=items(id,snippet,statistics)
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **videos** (array) - An array of video resources.
  - **id** (string) - The ID of the video.
  - **snippet** (object) - Contains details about the video's metadata.
    - **publishedAt** (string) - The date and time the video was published.
    - **channelId** (string) - The ID of the channel that published the video.
    - **title** (string) - The title of the video.
    - **description** (string) - The description of the video.
    - **thumbnails** (object) - Thumbnails for the video.
    - **categoryId** (string) - The ID of the video's category.
  - **statistics** (object) - Contains statistics about the video.
    - **viewCount** (string) - The number of views.
    - **likeCount** (string) - The number of likes.
    - **dislikeCount** (string) - The number of dislikes.
    - **favoriteCount** (string) - The number of favorites.
    - **commentCount** (string) - The number of comments.

#### Response Example
```json
{
 "videos": [
  {
   "id": "7lCDEYXw3mM",
   "snippet": {
    "publishedAt": "2012-06-20T22:45:24.000Z",
    "channelId": "UC_x5XG1OV2P6uZZ5FSM9Ttw",
    "title": "Google I/O 101: Q&A On Using Google APIs",
    "description": "Antonio Fuentes speaks to us and takes questions on working with Google APIs and OAuth 2.0.",

     "default": {

     },
     "medium": {
      "url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/mqdefault.jpg"
     },
     "high": {
      "url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/7lCDEYXw3mM/hqdefault.jpg"

## July 24, 2017 Release Notes

### Description
This update introduces a new quickstart guide for iOS developers and provides enhanced documentation for the YouTube Data API's interactive code snippet tool.

### Key Changes
- **iOS Quickstart Guide**: A new guide is available for integrating the YouTube Data API into iOS applications (Objective-C or Swift).
- **Code Snippet Tool Enhancements**: The interactive code snippet tool now includes documentation on:
  - Executing API requests.
  - Toggling between code snippets and full code samples.
  - Using boilerplate functions.
  - Loading existing resources for update methods.

### List My Channel Sections (HTTP)

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/docs/channelSections/list

This example shows how to retrieve channel sections for the authorized user's channel using an HTTP GET request. It uses the `mine` parameter set to `true` to indicate that the API should return sections for the authenticated user. The API call has a quota cost of 1 unit.

```http
GET https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/channelSections?mine=true&key=YOUR_API_KEY
```

### API Documentation and Code Samples Enhancements (April 4, 2019)

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=vi

Updates to the YouTube Data API v3 documentation and code samples, including the introduction of the APIs Explorer widget and updated quickstart guides.

```APIDOC
## API Documentation and Code Samples Enhancements (April 4, 2019)

### Description
This update enhances the API reference documentation for the YouTube Data API v3. It introduces the APIs Explorer widget for interactive API requests and provides a new 'Common use cases' section for clearer understanding. Code samples are now dynamically generated and available for Java, JavaScript, PHP, Python, and curl. The code samples tool has also been updated with a new UI offering similar features.

### Key Changes

*   **APIs Explorer Widget**: Allows users to select authorization scopes, enter sample parameter and property values, send API requests, and view responses. Offers a fullscreen view with dynamic code samples.
*   **Common Use Cases Section**: Added to API method documentation to explain typical use cases and provide links to populate the APIs Explorer with sample values.
*   **Updated Code Samples Tool**: Features a new UI with interactive exploration of use cases and dynamic code sample generation.
*   **Updated Quickstart Guides**: Revised guides for Java, JavaScript, PHP, and Python explain how to run samples using an API key or an OAuth 2.0 client ID.

### Supported Languages for Code Samples
- Java
- JavaScript
- PHP
- Python
- curl
```

### guideCategories.list - Error Handling

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=zh-tw

Handles 'notFound' error if a guide category cannot be found.

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/guideCategories/list

### Description
Retrieves a list of YouTube guide categories.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/guideCategories/list

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **id** (string) - Optional - The ID of the guide category to retrieve.

### Response
#### Error Response (404)
- **error.code** (integer) - 404
- **error.errors.reason** (string) - "notFound"
- **error.message** (string) - "The guide category identified by the id parameter cannot be found."

#### Response Example (Error)
{
  "error": {
    "code": 404,
    "errors": [
      {
        "reason": "notFound"
      }
    ],
    "message": "The guide category identified by the id parameter cannot be found."
  }
}
```

### GET /youtube/v3/videos - Deeply Filter Nested Response Fields

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/getting-started

This example demonstrates advanced usage of the 'fields' parameter to select specific nested properties within the 'snippet' object, alongside other top-level fields like 'statistics'.

```APIDOC
## GET /youtube/v3/videos

### Description
Retrieves a video resource, using the 'fields' parameter to select specific nested properties within the 'snippet' object and other top-level fields.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **id** (string) - Required - The ID of the video to retrieve.
- **key** (string) - Required - Your API key.
- **part** (string) - Required - Comma-separated list of resource parts to include in the response (e.g., snippet,statistics).
- **fields** (string) - Optional - Specifies which fields to return in the response (e.g., items(id,snippet(channelId,title,categoryId),statistics)).

### Request Example
```
GET https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos?id=7lCDEYXw3mM&key=YOUR_API_KEY&fields=items(id,snippet(channelId,title,categoryId),statistics)&part=snippet,statistics
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **videos** (array) - A list of video resources matching the request, with specified fields only.
  - **id** (string) - The ID of the video.
  - **snippet** (object) - The snippet object containing selected details about the video.
    - **channelId** (string) - The ID of the channel that published the video.
    - **title** (string) - The title of the video.
    - **categoryId** (string) - The ID of the video's category.
  - **statistics** (object) - The statistics object containing view, like, dislike, favorite, and comment counts.

#### Response Example
```json
{
 "videos": [
  {
   "id": "7lCDEYXw3mM",
   "snippet": {
    "channelId": "UC_x5XG1OV2P6uZZ5FSM9Ttw",
    "title": "Google I/O 101: Q&A On Using Google APIs",
    "categoryId": "28"

### Migration Guide Availability

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=th

A new guide was released on August 12, 2014, to help developers migrate their applications from the YouTube Data API v2 to the YouTube Data API v3.

```APIDOC
## YouTube Data API v2 to v3 Migration Guide

### Description
This guide provides instructions and best practices for migrating applications that currently use the YouTube Data API v2 to the latest version, YouTube Data API v3. The v2 API was officially deprecated on March 4, 2014.

### Access
The guide can be found at: [https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/migration-guide](https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/migration-guide)

### Target Audience
Developers who are currently using the YouTube Data API v2 and need to update their applications to the current API version.
```

### List Playlists for a Channel (Go)

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/code_samples/go

Demonstrates how to call the YouTube Data API v3's `playlists.list` method using Go. It requires command-line flags to specify parameters, such as the `channelId`. This example is part of a larger application that likely handles authentication and API interaction.

# Retrieve playlists for a specified channel

### Troubleshooting Broadcast Status Transitions

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/live/getting-started

Provides guidance on resolving issues related to broadcast status transitions, specifically when a broadcast gets stuck in intermediate statuses like 'testStarting' or 'liveStarting'.

```APIDOC
## Troubleshooting Broadcast Status Transitions

### Description
Guidelines for resolving problems when a broadcast's status transitions are delayed or stuck. It explains how YouTube handles status changes and the steps to take if a broadcast remains in an intermediate state.

### Method
N/A (This describes troubleshooting steps, not a direct API call)

### Endpoint
N/A

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
None

### Request Example
N/A

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
N/A

#### Response Example
N/A

### Troubleshooting Steps
- **Status Transitions:** When a broadcast transitions between statuses (e.g., `ready` to `testing`), YouTube may temporarily assign an intermediate status (e.g., `testStarting`) while completing associated actions.
- **Stuck Status:** If a broadcast becomes stuck in `testStarting` or `liveStarting` status:
  1. Call the `liveBroadcasts.delete` method to delete the broadcast.
  2. Create a new broadcast.
  3. Bind the new broadcast to your live stream.
  4. Continue with the testing process.
- **Prerequisite:** Before calling `liveBroadcasts.transition`, ensure the `status.streamStatus` property for the bound stream is `active`.
```

### Create YouTube Playlist and Add Video (C#)

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/code_samples/dotnet

This snippet uses the Google APIs Client Library for .NET to create a new playlist and add a video to it. It requires 'client_secrets.json' for authentication and the 'YouTubeService.Scope.Youtube' scope for full access. The output includes the IDs of the created playlist and playlist item.

```csharp
using System;
using System.IO;
using System.Reflection;
using System.Threading;
using System.Threading.Tasks;

using Google.Apis.Auth.OAuth2;
using Google.Apis.Services;
using Google.Apis.Upload;
using Google.Apis.Util.Store;
using Google.Apis.YouTube.v3;
using Google.Apis.YouTube.v3.Data;

namespace Google.Apis.YouTube.Samples
{
  /// <summary>
  /// YouTube Data API v3 sample: create a playlist.
  /// Relies on the Google APIs Client Library for .NET, v1.7.0 or higher.
  /// See https://developers.google.com/api-client-library/dotnet/get_started
  /// </summary>
  internal class PlaylistUpdates
  {
    [STAThread]
    static void Main(string[] args)
    {
      Console.WriteLine("YouTube Data API: Playlist Updates");
      Console.WriteLine("==================================");

      try
      {
        new PlaylistUpdates().Run().Wait();
      }
      catch (AggregateException ex)
      {
        foreach (var e in ex.InnerExceptions)
        {
          Console.WriteLine("Error: " + e.Message);
        }
      }

      Console.WriteLine("Press any key to continue...");
      Console.ReadKey();
    }

    private async Task Run()
    {
      UserCredential credential;
      using (var stream = new FileStream("client_secrets.json", FileMode.Open, FileAccess.Read))
      {
        credential = await GoogleWebAuthorizationBroker.AuthorizeAsync(
            GoogleClientSecrets.Load(stream).Secrets,
            // This OAuth 2.0 access scope allows for full read/write access to the
            // authenticated user's account.
            new[] { YouTubeService.Scope.Youtube },
            "user",
            CancellationToken.None,
            new FileDataStore(this.GetType().ToString())
        );
      }

      var youtubeService = new YouTubeService(new BaseClientService.Initializer() 
      {
        HttpClientInitializer = credential,
        ApplicationName = this.GetType().ToString()
      });

      // Create a new, private playlist in the authorized user's channel.
      var newPlaylist = new Playlist();
      newPlaylist.Snippet = new PlaylistSnippet();
      newPlaylist.Snippet.Title = "Test Playlist";
      newPlaylist.Snippet.Description = "A playlist created with the YouTube API v3";
      newPlaylist.Status = new PlaylistStatus();
      newPlaylist.Status.PrivacyStatus = "public";
      newPlaylist = await youtubeService.Playlists.Insert(newPlaylist, "snippet,status").ExecuteAsync();

      // Add a video to the newly created playlist.
      var newPlaylistItem = new PlaylistItem();
      newPlaylistItem.Snippet = new PlaylistItemSnippet();
      newPlaylistItem.Snippet.PlaylistId = newPlaylist.Id;
      newPlaylistItem.Snippet.ResourceId = new ResourceId();
      newPlaylistItem.Snippet.ResourceId.Kind = "youtube#video";
      newPlaylistItem.Snippet.ResourceId.VideoId = "GNRMeaz6QRI";
      newPlaylistItem = await youtubeService.PlaylistItems.Insert(newPlaylistItem, "snippet").ExecuteAsync();

      Console.WriteLine("Playlist item id {0} was added to playlist id {1}.", newPlaylistItem.Id, newPlaylist.Id);
    }
  }
}

```

### Create Playlist

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/code_samples/dotnet

Demonstrates how to create a private playlist using the `playlists.insert` method. The authenticated channel will own the playlist and can add videos to it.

```APIDOC
## POST /youtube/v3/playlists

### Description
Creates a private playlist for the authenticated channel and optionally adds a video to it.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/playlists

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **part** (string) - Required - The part parameter specifies the playlist properties that the API response should include. Set to "snippet" to include these.

#### Request Body
- **snippet.title** (string) - Required - The title of the playlist.
- **snippet.description** (string) - Optional - The description of the playlist.
- **status.privacyStatus** (string) - Required - Privacy status of the playlist. Acceptable values are "private", "public", and "unlisted".
- **items[0].snippet.resourceId.kind** (string) - Optional - The kind of resource to associate with the playlist item. Acceptable values are "youtube#video".
- **items[0].resourceId.videoId** (string) - Optional - The video ID to add to the playlist.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "snippet": {
    "title": "My Awesome Playlist",
    "description": "A playlist of my favorite videos."
  },
  "status": {
    "privacyStatus": "private"
  },
  "items": [
    {
      "snippet": {
        "resourceId": {
          "kind": "youtube#video",
          "videoId": "dQw4w9WgXcQ"
        }
      }
    }
  ]
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **id** (string) - The unique ID of the created playlist.
- **snippet** (object) - The snippet object contains basic details about the playlist.
- **status** (object) - The status object contains privacy information about the playlist.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "kind": "youtube#playlist",
  "etag": "_abcdefg1234567890",
  "id": "PLabcdefg1234567890",
  "snippet": {
    "publishedAt": "2023-01-01T12:00:00Z",
    "channelId": "UCxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx",
    "title": "My Awesome Playlist",
    "description": "A playlist of my favorite videos.",
    "thumbnails": {
      "default": {
        "url": "https://i.ytimg.com/vi/abcdefg123/default.jpg",
        "width": 120,
        "height": 90
      }
    },
    "channelTitle": "Example Channel",
    "localized": {
      "title": "My Awesome Playlist",
      "description": "A playlist of my favorite videos."
    }
  },
  "status": {
    "privacyStatus": "private"
  }
}
```
```

### Get OAuth2 Token from User Prompt (Go)

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/code_samples/go

Prompts the user to open an authorization URL in their browser and then enter the received authorization code on the command line. It uses the provided OAuth2 configuration to exchange this code for an access token. This method is suitable for interactive command-line applications.

```go
// getTokenFromPrompt uses Config to request a Token and prompts the user
// to enter the token on the command line. It returns the retrieved Token.
func getTokenFromPrompt(config *oauth2.Config, authURL string) (*oauth2.Token, error) {
	var code string
	fmt.Printf("Go to the following link in your browser. After completing " +
		"the authorization flow, enter the authorization code on the command " +
		"line: \n%v\n", authURL)

	if _, err := fmt.Scan(&code); err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Unable to read authorization code %v", err)
	}
	fmt.Println(authURL)
	return exchangeToken(config, code)
}
```

### Python Example for channels.update Method

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=tr

Shows how to update channel settings using Python and the YouTube Data API v3. This snippet focuses on the channels.update method, including the use of onBehalfOfContentOwner.

```Python
from googleapiclient.discovery import build

# Assume 'youtube' is an authenticated YouTube API service object
youtube = build('youtube', 'v3', developerKey='YOUR_API_KEY') # Replace with your authenticated client

channel_id = 'UCxxxxxxxxxxxxxx' # Replace with your channel ID

channel_update_body = {
    'brandingSettings': {
        'channel': {
            'unsubscribedTrailer': 'VIDEO_ID_HERE' # Replace with a public or unlisted video ID
        }
    }
}

request = youtube.channels().update(
    id=channel_id,
    part='brandingSettings',
    body=channel_update_body,
    onBehalfOfContentOwner='YOUR_CONTENT_OWNER_ID' # Optional: Only if updating on behalf of a content owner
)

try:
    response = request.execute()
    print("Channel updated successfully:", response)
except Exception as e:
    print(f"An error occurred: {e}")

```

### Search YouTube by Keyword using YouTube V3 API (Go)

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/code_samples/go

This snippet demonstrates how to search for YouTube content (videos, channels, playlists) based on a keyword. It utilizes the `search.list` method and requires a developer key for authentication. The results are categorized and printed to the console. Dependencies include `flag`, `fmt`, `log`, `net/http`, `google.golang.org/api/googleapi/transport`, and `google.golang.org/api/youtube/v3`.

```Go
package main

import (
	"flag"
	"fmt"
	"log"
	"net/http"

	"google.golang.org/api/googleapi/transport"
	"google.golang.org/api/youtube/v3"
)

var (
	query      = flag.String("query", "Google", "Search term")
	maxResults = flag.Int64("max-results", 25, "Max YouTube results")
)

const developerKey = "YOUR DEVELOPER KEY"

func main() {
	flag.Parse()

	client := &http.Client{
		Transport: &transport.APIKey{Key: developerKey},
	}

	service, err := youtube.New(client)
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error creating new YouTube client: %v", err)
	}

	// Make the API call to YouTube.
	call := service.Search.List("id,snippet").
		Q(*query).
		MaxResults(*maxResults)
	response, err := call.Do()
	handleError(err, "")

	// Group video, channel, and playlist results in separate lists.

videos := make(map[string]string)

channels := make(map[string]string)

playlists := make(map[string]string)

	// Iterate through each item and add it to the correct list.
	for _, item := range response.Items {
		switch item.Id.Kind {
		case "youtube#video":
		
videos[item.Id.VideoId] = item.Snippet.Title
		case "youtube#channel":
		
channels[item.Id.ChannelId] = item.Snippet.Title
		case "youtube#playlist":
		
playlists[item.Id.PlaylistId] = item.Snippet.Title
		}
	}

	printIDs("Videos", videos)
	printIDs("Channels", channels)
	printIDs("Playlists", playlists)
}

// Print the ID and title of each result in a list as well as a name that
// identifies the list. For example, print the word section name "Videos"
// above a list of video search results, followed by the video ID and title
// of each matching video.
func printIDs(sectionName string, matches map[string]string) {
	fmt.Printf("%v:\n", sectionName)
	for id, title := range matches {
		fmt.Printf("[%v] %v\n", id, title)
	}
	fmt.Printf("\n\n")
}

search_by_keyword.go

```

--------------------------------

### Java Example for thumbnails.set Method

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=tr

Provides a Java code sample for setting custom thumbnails for videos using the YouTube Data API v3. This snippet showcases the thumbnails.set method.

```Java
import com.google.api.client.googleapis.json.GoogleJsonResponseException;
import com.google.api.client.http.InputStreamContent;
import com.google.api.services.youtube.YouTube;
import com.google.api.services.youtube.model.ThumbnailSetResponse;

import java.io.FileInputStream;
import java.io.IOException;
import java.io.InputStream;

public class SetThumbnail {

    /**
     * Sets a custom thumbnail for a video.
     * 
     * @param youtube The YouTube API client.
     * @param videoId The ID of the video to set the thumbnail for.
     * @param filePath The path to the thumbnail image file.
     */
    public static void setVideoThumbnail(YouTube youtube, String videoId, String filePath) {
        InputStreamContent mediaContent = null;
        try {
            InputStream thumbnailStream = new FileInputStream(filePath);
            mediaContent = new InputStreamContent("image/png", thumbnailStream);
            mediaContent.setLength(thumbnailStream.available());
        } catch (IOException e) {
            System.err.println("Error reading thumbnail file: " + e.getMessage());
            return;
        }

        try {
            YouTube.Thumbnails.Set request = youtube.thumbnails().set(videoId, mediaContent);
            ThumbnailSetResponse response = request.execute();
            System.out.println("Thumbnail set successfully for video " + videoId + ": " + response);
        } catch (GoogleJsonResponseException e) {
            System.err.println("GoogleJsonResponseException setVideoThumbnail: " + e.getDetails().getMessage());
            e.printStackTrace();
        } catch (IOException e) {
            System.err.println("IOException setVideoThumbnail: " + e.getMessage());
            e.printStackTrace();
        }
    }

    // Example usage (assuming you have an authenticated YouTube object named 'youtube'):
    // public static void main(String[] args) {
    //     // Initialize your YouTube object here
    //     YouTube youtube = ...;
    //     String videoId = "YOUR_VIDEO_ID";
    //     String thumbnailPath = "path/to/your/thumbnail.png";
    //     setVideoThumbnail(youtube, videoId, thumbnailPath);
    // }
}
```

### Get OAuth2 Token from Web Server Flow (Go)

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/code_samples/go

Initiates a local web server to handle the OAuth2 callback, then opens the authorization URL in the user's default browser. It waits for the web server to receive the authorization code and then exchanges it for an access token. This method automates the authorization process for applications with a web interface or those that can run a local server.

```go
// getTokenFromWeb uses Config to request a Token.
// It returns the retrieved Token.
func getTokenFromWeb(config *oauth2.Config, authURL string) (*oauth2.Token, error) {
	codeCh, err := startWebServer()
	if err != nil {
		fmt.Printf("Unable to start a web server.")
		return nil, err
	}

	err = openURL(authURL)
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Unable to open authorization URL in web server: %v", err)
	} else {
		fmt.Println("Your browser has been opened to an authorization URL.",
			" This program will resume once authorization has been provided.\n")
		fmt.Println(authURL)
	}

	// Wait for the web server to get the code.
	code := <-codeCh
	return exchangeToken(config, code)
}
```

### Retrieve My Uploads using .NET Client Library

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/docs/playlistItems/list

This .NET code sample retrieves a list of videos uploaded to the authenticated user's channel by calling the `playlistItems.list` and `channels.list` methods. It uses the Google APIs Client Library for .NET.

```csharp
using System;
using System.IO;
using System.Reflection;
using System.Threading;
using System.Threading.Tasks;

using Google.Apis.Auth.OAuth2;
using Google.Apis.Services;
using Google.Apis.Upload;
using Google.Apis.Util.Store;
using Google.Apis.YouTube.v3;
using Google.Apis.YouTube.v3.Data;

namespace Google.Apis.YouTube.Samples
{
  /// <summary>
  /// YouTube Data API v3 sample: retrieve my uploads.
  /// Relies on the Google APIs Client Library for .NET, v1.7.0 or higher.
  /// See https://developers.google.com/api-client-library/dotnet/get_started
  /// </summary>
  internal class MyUploads
  {
    [STAThread]
    static void Main(string[] args)
    {
      Console.WriteLine("YouTube Data API: My Uploads");
      Console.WriteLine("============================");

      try
      {
        new MyUploads().Run().Wait();
      }
      catch (AggregateException ex)
      {
        foreach (var e in ex.InnerExceptions)
        {
          Console.WriteLine("Error: " + e.Message);
        }
      }

      Console.WriteLine("Press any key to continue...");
      Console.ReadKey();
    }

    private async Task Run()
    {
      UserCredential credential;
      using (var stream = new FileStream("client_secrets.json", FileMode.Open, FileAccess.Read))
      {
        credential = await GoogleWebAuthorizationBroker.AuthorizeAsync(
            GoogleClientSecrets.Load(stream).Secrets,
            // This OAuth 2.0 access scope allows for read-only access to the authenticated 
            // user's account, but not other types of account access.
            new[] { YouTubeService.Scope.YoutubeReadonly },
            "user",
            CancellationToken.None,
            new FileDataStore(this.GetType().ToString())
        );
      }

      var youtubeService = new YouTubeService(new BaseClientService.Initializer()
      {
        HttpClientInitializer = credential,
        ApplicationName = this.GetType().ToString()
      });

      var channelsListRequest = youtubeService.Channels.List("contentDetails");
      channelsListRequest.Mine = true;

      // Retrieve the contentDetails part of the channel resource for the authenticated user's channel.

```

### Retrieve Video Resource with Specific Parts (YouTube Data API v3)

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/getting-started

This example demonstrates how to retrieve a video resource using the YouTube Data API v3. It specifies the 'part' parameter to include 'snippet', 'contentDetails', 'statistics', and 'status' in the response. The 'fields' parameter is not used, so default properties like 'kind' and 'etag' are included.

```URL
https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/videos?id=7lCDEYXw3mM&key=YOUR_API_KEY&part=snippet,contentDetails,statistics,status
```

--------------------------------

### YouTube API: Search List (Go)

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=vi

Provides a Go example for performing searches using the YouTube Data API v3. This allows searching for videos, channels, and playlists based on various criteria.

```Go
package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"log"

	"google.golang.org/api/youtube/v3"
)

func main() {
	// Assume client is an authorized *http.Client
	sservice, err := youtube.New(client)
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error creating YouTube client: %v", err)
	}

	call := service.Search.List("snippet")
	call.Q("Google Developers") // Search query
	call.Type("video")         // Search for videos
	call.MaxResults(10)        // Number of results

	response, err := call.Do()
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Error making API call to search: %v", err)
	}

	fmt.Printf("Search results: %+v\n", response.Items)
}

```

### playlistItems.insert and videos.rate

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=tr

The playlistItems.insert method's Python example was removed as its functionality is now handled by the videos.rate method.

```APIDOC
## POST /youtube/v3/playlistItems

### Description
This endpoint is used for inserting items into a playlist. The Python example for this method has been updated.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/playlistItems

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **part** (string) - Required - The part parameter specifies the playlist items that you want to retrieve. The following fields are valid:
  - snippet
  - contentDetails

### Request Body
- **snippet.playlistId** (string) - Required - The playlist ID to insert the item into.
- **snippet.resourceId.kind** (string) - Required - The kind of resource being referenced. The value is youtube#video.
- **snippet.resourceId.videoId** (string) - Required - The video ID to insert into the playlist.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "snippet": {
    "playlistId": "PL...",
    "resourceId": {
      "kind": "youtube#video",
      "videoId": "..."
    }
  }
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **kind** (string) - The kind of resource, defaulting to youtube#playlistItem.
- **etag** (string) - Etag of the playlist item.
- **snippet** (object) - The snippet object contains details about the playlist item.
- **contentDetails** (object) - The contentDetails object contains details about the playlist item.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "kind": "youtube#playlistItem",
  "etag": "...",
  "snippet": {
    "publishedAt": "2023-01-01T00:00:00Z",
    "channelId": "UC...",
    "title": "Video Title",
    "description": "Video Description",
    "thumbnails": {},
    "channelTitle": "Channel Title",
    "videoOwnerChannelId": "UC...",
    "videoOwnerChannelTitle": "Channel Title",
    "position": 0,
    "playlistId": "PL..."
  },
  "contentDetails": {
    "videoId": "...",
    "startAt": "0",
    "endAt": ""
  }
}
```

## POST /youtube/v3/videos

### Description
This endpoint is used for rating videos. This method now handles the functionality previously demonstrated by the playlistItems.insert method's Python example.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
/youtube/v3/videos

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **id** (string) - Required - The ID of the video to rate.
- **rating** (string) - Required - The rating to apply to the video. Valid values are: like, dislike, none.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "id": "...",
  "rating": "like"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **id** (string) - The ID of the video that was rated.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "id": "..."
}
```
```

### Retrieve My Uploads

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/code_samples/ruby

This example demonstrates how to retrieve a list of videos uploaded to a channel associated with the authenticated request. It utilizes the `playlistItems.list` and `channels.list` methods.

```APIDOC
## Retrieve my uploads

This sample calls the API's `playlistItems.list` method to retrieve a list of videos uploaded to the channel associated with the request. The code also calls the `channels.list` method with the `mine` parameter set to `true` to retrieve the playlist ID that identifies the channel's uploaded videos.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
`/youtube/v3/playlistItems` (used in conjunction with `/youtube/v3/channels`)

### Description
Retrieves a list of videos uploaded by the authenticated user's channel.

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **part** (string) - Required - Specifies the parts of the playlist item to retrieve (e.g., 'snippet').
- **playlistId** (string) - Required - The ID of the playlist that contains the channel's uploaded videos. This is obtained by calling `channels.list` with `mine=true`.
- **mine** (boolean) - Required (for `channels.list` call) - Set to `true` to retrieve information about the authenticated user's channel.

### Request Example
```ruby
#!/usr/bin/ruby

require 'rubygems'
gem 'google-api-client', '>0.7'
require 'google/api_client'
require 'google/api_client/client_secrets'
require 'google/api_client/auth/file_storage'
require 'google/api_client/auth/installed_app'

# ... (authentication setup code)

# Call channels.list to get the uploads playlist ID
channel_response = client.execute(
  :api_method => youtube.channels,
  :parameters => {'mine' => 'true'}
)

uploads_playlist_id = channel_response.data.items[0].content_details.related_playlists.uploads

# Call playlistItems.list to get the videos in the uploads playlist
playlist_response = client.execute(
  :api_method => youtube.playlist_items,
  :parameters => {
    'part' => 'snippet',
    'playlistId' => uploads_playlist_id
  }
)

# Process playlist_response.data.items to get video details
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **items** (array) - A list of playlist item resources, each containing details about an uploaded video.
  - **snippet** (object) - Contains details about the video, such as title, description, and thumbnails.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "kind": "youtube#playlistItemListResponse",
  "etag": "...",
  "items": [
    {
      "kind": "youtube#playlistItem",
      "etag": "...",
      "id": "...",
      "snippet": {
        "publishedAt": "2023-01-01T10:00:00Z",
        "channelId": "...",
        "title": "My Awesome Video",
        "description": "This is a description of my video.",
        "thumbnails": {
          "default": {"url": "..."},
          "medium": {"url": "..."},
          "high": {"url": "..."}
        },
        "playlistId": "...",
        "position": 0,
        "resourceId": {
          "kind": "youtube#video",
          "videoId": "..."
        }
      }
    }
    // ... more items
  ]
}
```
```

### Python Authorization Flow for Installed Apps with YouTube Data API

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/revision_history_hl=zh-tw

This Python code sample demonstrates the authorization flow for installed applications using the google-auth and google-auth-oauthlib libraries. It replaces the deprecated oauth2client library and is designed to be run locally. This flow is suitable for desktop or mobile applications.

```Python
from google_auth_oauthlib.flow import InstalledAppFlow

# Scopes define the level of access the application requests.
SCOPES = ['https://www.googleapis.com/auth/youtube.force-ssl']
API_SERVICE_NAME = 'youtube'
API_VERSION = 'v3'

def get_authenticated_service():
    flow = InstalledAppFlow.from_client_secrets_file(
        'client_secrets.json', scopes=SCOPES)
    credentials = flow.run_local_server(port=0)
    # The youtube client is built using the googleapiclient.discovery.build()
    # function, which takes the API service name and version as arguments.
    return discovery.build(API_SERVICE_NAME, API_VERSION, credentials=credentials)

if __name__ == '__main__':
    youtube = get_authenticated_service()
    # Example usage: list channels
    request = youtube.channels().list(
        part="snippet,contentDetails,statistics",
        mine=True
    )
    response = request.execute()
    print(response)
```

### GET /channels - List channel data by YouTube handle

Source: https://developers.google.com/youtube/v3/code_samples/code_snippets

Retrieves channel data for a specific YouTube channel using its YouTube handle.

```APIDOC
## GET /channels

### Description
Retrieves channel data for a specific YouTube channel using its YouTube handle.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/channels

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **forHandle** (string) - Required - The YouTube handle for which to retrieve information.
- **part** (string) - Optional - Specifies the channel resource parts that the API response should include.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "example": "GET https://www.googleapis.com/youtube/v3/channels?part=snippet&forHandle=@GoogleDevelopers"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **items** (array) - Contains channel resource objects.
  - **snippet** (object) - Contains basic information about the channel.
    - **title** (string) - The title of the channel.
    - **description** (string) - The channel's description.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "example": {
    "kind": "youtube#channelListResponse",
    "etag": "...",
    "items": [
      {
        "kind": "youtube#channel",
        "etag": "...",
        "id": "UC_x5XG1OV2P6uZZ5FSM9Ttw",
        "snippet": {
          "title": "Google for Developers",
          "description": "Official YouTube channel for Google for Developers."
        }
      }
    ]
  }
}
```
```
